The Syllogism
intermediate
10 min
Qiyas al-Khalf: Reductio ad Absurdum in Islamic Logic
Author defines and exemplifies reductio ad absurdum.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the method of qiyas al-khalf to refute a false premise in a categorical syllogism and derive the true contradictory.

Core Idea
Qiyas al-khalf proves a proposition by showing its negation leads to absurdity.

This lesson introduces the method of reductio ad absurdum (qiyas al-khalf) as presented by al-Ghazali. You will see how a manifestly false conclusion forces us to reject an opponent's premise, thereby establishing the truth of its opposite. This method is essential in kalām for refuting false doctrines.

Guided Path
1
Identify the opponent's claim
Start with the proposition you want to refute. In the example, the opponent claims 'the world is eternal'. This will be your minor premise.
The opponent's claim is assumed as a hypothesis to be tested.
2
Add a manifestly true premise
Combine the opponent's claim with a premise that is accepted as true by all parties. Here, 'Everything eternal is not composed' is obvious.
This premise must be undeniable; otherwise, the argument loses force.
3
Derive the conclusion
From these two premises, construct a categorical syllogism. The example yields: 'Therefore, the world is not composed.'
Use the first figure for direct deduction.
4
Recognize the absurdity
The conclusion is manifestly false (the world is composed). Since the argument is valid, at least one premise must be false.
If the conclusion is false, the premises cannot both be true.
5
Identify and negate the false premise
The true premise (eternals are not composed) is accepted, so the false premise is the opponent's claim. Therefore, its contradictory (the world is not eternal) is true.
This is the desired conclusion: the opposite of the opponent's claim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسألة. ونظيره من نقيضه، وهو أنه ليس بفرض، صادقاً وهو المطلوب من العقليات :قولنا كلّ ما هو أزلي فلا يكون مؤلفاً، والعالم أزلي فإذن لا يكون مؤلّفاً، لكن النتيجة ظاهرة الكذب ففي المقدمات كاذبة. وقولنا : الأزلي ليس بمؤلف ظاهر الصدق فينحصر الكذب في قولنا : العالم أزلي، فإذن نقيضه وهو أن العالم ليس بأزلي صدق وهو المطلوب؛ فطريق هذا القياس أن تأخذ مذهب الخصم وتجعله مقدمة وتضيف إليها مقدمة أخرى ظاهرة الصدق، فينتج من القياس نتيجة ظاهرة الكذب فتبيّن أن ذلك لوجود كاذبة في المقدمات. ويجوز يُسمّى هذا قياس الخلف، لأنك ترجع من النتيجة إلى الخلف، فتأخذ مطلوبك من المقدمة التي خلفتها كأنها مُسلّمة، ويجوز أن يُسمّى قياس الخلف لأن الخلف هو الكذب المناقض للصدق، وقد أدرجت في المقدمات كاذبة في معرض الصدق، ولا مشاحة في التسمية بعد فهم المعنى
The issue. Its counterpart from its opposite, and it is that it is not a duty, true, and that is the desired from intellectual matters: our saying: everything that is eternal is not composed, and the world is eternal, therefore it is not composed, but the conclusion is manifestly false, so the premises are false. And our saying: the eternal is not composed is manifestly true, so the falsehood is confined to our saying: the world is eternal, therefore its opposite, that the world is not eternal, is true, and that is the desired. So the way of this syllogism is that you take the opponent's view and make it a premise, and add to it another premise that is manifestly true, then from the syllogism results a conclusion that is manifestly false, so it becomes clear that that is due to the existence of a falsehood in the premises. And this may be called qiyas al-khalf (syllogism of contradiction), because you return from the conclusion to the contradiction, so you take your desired from the premise that you left behind as if it were conceded, and it may be called qiyas al-khalf because the khalf (contradiction) is the falsehood that contradicts truth, and you have inserted into the premises a falsehood under the guise of truth, and there is no dispute over the name after understanding the meaning.
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage explains the method of reductio ad absurdum, which Al-Ghazali calls qiyas al-khalf. The author begins by illustrating it with an intellectual example: if we say 'Everything eternal is not composed; the world is eternal; therefore the world is not composed', but the conclusion is known false, then at least one premise must be false. Since 'the eternal is not composed' is manifestly true, the false premise must be 'the world is eternal'. Therefore its opposite, 'the world is not eternal', is true, which is the desired conclusion. The author then generalises the method: take the opponent's claim as a premise, combine it with an obviously true premise, and if the result is an absurd conclusion, then the opponent's premise is false. He explains that this is called qiyas al-khalf because you go back from the absurd result to the contradictory premise, and also because 'khalf' means falsehood contrary to truth. The author notes that terminology is not important once the meaning is understood.

Key Terms
قياس الخلف
خلف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a reductio ad absurdum, what is the logical status of the premise taken from the opponent?
A) It is known to be true.
B) It is assumed as a hypothesis to be refuted.
C) It is the conclusion of a previous syllogism.
D) It is necessarily false.

Key Takeaway
Qiyas al-khalf is a method of proof that refutes a false claim by showing its entailment of an absurdity, thereby establishing the truth of its opposite.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Using qiyas al-khalf, refute the claim that there are two gods. Assume the opponent's premise: 'There are two gods (A and B)'. Combine with the true premise: 'If there were two gods, they would disagree on the creation of the universe'. Then: 'Disagreement leads to corruption (fasad)'. But we observe: 'The universe is not corrupt'. Therefore, the assumption is false, so the contradictory 'There is only one God' is true.
?
Identify the false premise in the following argument: 'Everything that is eternal is necessary; the world is eternal; therefore the world is necessary.' If the world is known to be contingent, use qiyas al-khalf to determine which premise is false and state the correct conclusion.
